O, my children, now I have completed this book, which is the last of the science of medicine. By its completion at the end and by its exposition, and by its explanations, it seems to me that I have rendered comprehensible to you the treatise which pertains to my practice, namely surgery.
For surgery in our region and in our time has been almost entirely deprived, except that the science of it was somewhat visible, and its traces remained; but we would know little about it beyond small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have altered many things and led to errors and hesitation due to their obscure expressions and weakened strength of the art.
And it seems to me that I should enliven this treatise according to the method of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and so that it may come with the forms of cautery tools and other instruments of the work as is necessary through addition of explanation and preparation, which cause is essential.
But the reason why a good practitioner is not easily found in our profession in this time is that the art of medicine is extensive, and one must be trained in the science of anatomy, which involves knowing the functions of the members and their forms, as well as their connections and separations; and having knowledge of the bones, nerves, and ligaments, their numbers, and their positions; and of the pulsating veins and the static ones, and the places for their incisions.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that in name it is much, but in practice little, and even less in the art of the hand.
We have already said this at the beginning of this book; for whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said about anatomy will inevitably fall into error through which men may die, as I have seen too many of them, for some are formed in this science and get themselves out of that with no knowledge or experience.
For I saw a foolish doctor who had incised an abscess in the neck of a woman, and he cut into some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed out, and the woman died as a result.
And I saw another doctor who attempted to remove a stone from a man who was suffering from bladder stones, and the stone was large. He came to him and extracted that stone along with part of the bladder, whereupon that man died on the third day.
And I had already called to remove that stone and saw that because of the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I knew beyond a doubt that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was receiving payment from a duke of our land to perform surgery. He came to a black castrated man who had a fracture in his thigh; and due to the doctor's ignorance, he removed the plaster over the fracture before it was ready, applying poultices and splints with too much force, not allowing the wound proper healing time.
And he loosened it according to his desires, and soon after he relieved him, and after some days commanded us to remove the bandage. And thus it was that the thigh and leg became abscessed, and he came to ruin.
And I was called to attend him, and I prepared to remove the bandage. Achieving some relief, he was thus freed from his pains.
However, once the corruption was confirmed in the limb, so that it could not be restrained, and the corruption did not cease to spread throughout the limb until the patient's danger increased.
And I saw another doctor who incised a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated near the armpit, until the malignancy greatly revealed its evil nature to lord so-and-so.
The cause of this is that the malignant condition is pure of melancholic humor; therefore, it does not need to affect all parts equally, but rather it affects the member which can withstand being its host.
And for this reason, children, it is necessary for you that the operation be planned in two aspects: one is an operation associated with health, and the other is work in which there is risk even under the best conditions.
And I have already discussed this in every part of this book where there is an operation involving error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to guard against that and leave aside this, so that the pages do not lead me to speak and thus dishonor you.
And so take up your arms with diligence and the protection of God, and your patients with skill and firmness.
And use the best path by God's grace to lead to health and praiseworthy success, and leave behind terrible diseases that are difficult to heal, and keep your weapons away from what causes you fear, so that hesitation does not undermine your faith and reputation: for more remains for your glory, and after in the world and finally to your sanctity.
Wound treatment in some monastic surgeries: Do not treat illness badly, for thus bad doctors are not named.
And I have dedicated this book according to three chapters.
The division of the book begins, and first of the first part. The first chapter is ordered regarding the head and neck, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cautery, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, concerning incision and puncture, and of cupping, and of plasters, and of the extraction of arrows and similar things, fully chaptered and ordered regarding the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, concerning restoration and dislocation, and the treatment of twists and similar conditions; a chapter ordered regarding the head and neck, and the forms of the instruments.
I will speak of the quality of the movements of that cautery and of its instruments, and in what condition cautery should be prohibited.
Therefore, I say that the speech about the quality of the movement of cautery and of its instrument is long and verbose, subtle by science, and hidden as a secret; many wise men have spoken much about it, and they are discordant among themselves, but for me a little of their speeches suffices, fearing to be protracted.
Therefore, I say that cauteries conform to all complete formations universally, whether they are made of material or immaterial substances, with the exception of two formations, which are tail-like formations without material substance.
In the tail-like and dry formation made of material, it dries out; for some say that cauteries are helpful in this case, while others say the opposite, that cauteries are not suitable for a disease which is due to quality and dryness, since the nature of fire is hot and dry, and it is inappropriate that a tail-like and dry disease be treated with something that is hot and dry.
And those who say the opposite are mistaken, that cauteries are beneficial in every tail-like and dry disease that occurs in human bodies, for when you compare the human body and its humidity to the nature of fire, you find that the human body is more fragile.
And I say according to the words of that person, that through experience I have already discovered this myself on several occasions.
But it does not suit him who has already been trained and exercised in the chapter of cauteries through previous practice, and who has known the diversity of human constitutions and the disposition of diseases in their seasons, as well as their causes and accidents, and the time span of them.
But in other formations, there is no need for fear on your part, especially in fragile and humid diseases, since all doctors are now in agreement about these, and they do not disagree regarding the use of cauteries in them.
And know, children, that the secret of healing by cauteries with fire and its goodness lies in the fact that fire is simple, and its action affects only the member being cauterized and does not harm other members adjacent to it except for slight discomfort.
Here is the English translation:
Take the fire, by its elevation and goodness of substance, it does nothing but superfluify [sic], and already it is known to us through experiment and length of service in studying the art regarding the truth of causes; and for this I excuse myself from the length of speech. And if not that it were not read in my book at this place hidden secrets with fire, and the quality of its operation on bodies and the expulsion process by which you expel diseases, in a philosophical demonstrative speech, which would be sharp in your possessions.
And know, children, that they disagree about the time when it is appropriate to perform cautery and pause at the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, for the harm caused by accidental circumstances is submerged in the benefit of what is attracted through cautery, and especially if the cautery is performed due to necessary pains or inflammations, which cannot tolerate delay because it is feared that such conditions could lead to greater malice, which is worse than a small harm entering with the times.
And this does not concern your possessions, or, children, what is valued only by the common people and foolish doctors, is that for the disease which is cured by cautery it is not suitable at all times, and they pause at the consequence.
And the reason is not thus because they think about it, for cautery is nothing but a substitute for medicine that alters the complexion and dries up the humidities which are the cause of the pains.
But yet, cautery surpasses medicine in terms of the speed of its effectiveness and the virtue of its operation and the greatness of its lord.
It is possible that his illness may return at some time according to the patient's constitution and the location of his illness, and its nature, and what has been prepared in his body by the aggregation of superfluities in him, and what has reached him through his acquisition in food and similar causes; but if it is a subtle illness with few superfluities and humidities, such as cautery for toothache and similar cases, it may not return that pain, but this applies to small matters.
And the common saying is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is the saying of a craftsman, not what those who understand it say, for I believe there is no cure that benefits either from medicine or any other cause before applying cautery.
And the cause is contrary to that; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when administering methods of treatment for certain illnesses, where other medicines are ineffective, and at the end of the cause, one applies cautery, and it benefits in such cases. And here from what was said before that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the understanding which I understand of the common and faults of foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the subtlety of its substance.
And they said that the location for cautery does not matter, which is not absolutely true, because I have experienced this and have found that it works differently on different bodies; cautery with gold can be better than with iron as others claim. However, when you use fire to apply gold for cautery, it is not clear how much to prepare, since the hardness of gold requires proper adjustment; if you set it over fire, the gold will melt due to the heat, and placing some plates in the fire helps the craftsman work with it.
And thus is made the cautery of iron, which should be applied lightly and gradually according to the correctness of the procedure.
And I have already arranged this chapter on cauteries according to the chapters, and I have placed those for the head among the parts, so that I alleviate the seeker who asks for what they desire.
The first chapter.
This cautery is applied to the humidity and coldness that cause accidental headaches due to these two causes, which are caused by sweating and a large amount of rheumatic flux, called coryza, affecting the head and ears, as well as excessive sleepiness, toothache, and throat pain, and generally all illnesses that come from coldness, such as paralysis, stroke, and similar conditions.
The form of this cautery is as follows: first, command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine for the head cleansing, for three or four nights, according to what you deem necessary based on the strength of the patient and their age and habit.
And then command him to shave his head with a razor, and then place him to sit on a reclined bench and have him rest his head on his own hands.
And then place the palm of your hand above the nose, between the eyebrows, on the shaved area. But when the heat of your hand has reached that place, mark that spot with a needle, and then apply the olive wood cautery, which is made as follows:
And then pause that which is sewn with thread, in such a way that it descends, with the membrane of which the wound must be gradually constricted, and you turn it.
And then lift your hand gently and look at the place, and if you see any quantity of bone already exposed, as much as the quantity of grain in one ear of corn, then raise your hand, and if not return your hand to that tool, or another like it, if it is cold, until you can feel the bone which I have told you about.
And then take a little salt and dissolve it over the place and let it be for three days.
And then sew around the wound embedded at the edge and let it be inside until the burn scar is destroyed. And then treat the place with a quadruple ointment until it is healed.
And they say that when the plague ulcer opens spontaneously, it is better and more helpful to let the arm be so.
And some of them say that the cord should be cauterized to the bone, and that the cautery should remain until it adheres to some part of the bone.
And then remove what is adhered to the bone, and then it should be treated.
And others say that with the cautery it should reach to the deepest part, until it presses strongly against the bone until the bone melts, and this is the method of alpechini (small burns): And they believe that from that place the vapors of the head emanate.
And let the wound be treated for a long time until it is healed and has consolidated.
I have not seen these two types of cautery used generally on everyone out of fear; and leave that one alone, for me it is better to be healthy without it. For the head is delicate because of the solution of continuity of its veins as we have testified in other parts of the body, especially when the nature of the patient's head is weak.
And the first type of cautery is safer and better for me; and with that one I can work more safely.
Chapter Second.
About cauterization of the head.
When chronic and long-lasting pain occurs throughout the head, and this is prolonged in the patient despite the use of plasters, compresses, decoctions, poultices, ointments, and other remedies, especially if cauterization with a previously used cautery has not been beneficial for any of these causes, then consider whether the patient's head is of strong constitution and not weak. If there is no significant tenderness, proceed to cauterize with another type of cautery below that one slightly. And then cauterize that area above the crown of their head with a cautery until the pain is relieved. Cut the pain and expose the bone in the quantity that we have described, and cauterize that area with a cautery at the back of the head in the place called "vas," which is where the vein is located. And take care in this, and do not expose the bone, for the patient from this would discover great pain different from the pain of all other cauteries of the head.
And here I will describe this cautery in its place, for it is fitting that the cautery with which you cauterize the horns of the head and the occiput is a finer cautery than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Three.
On Cauterization of Recent Wounds.
When severe pain is found in the upper part of the head, or if there is persistent pain within the skull, it should be evacuated with medicines that purify the head, and the other treatment which I have described for diseases should be administered; and if this does not benefit, then cauterization is done in two ways: either cauterization with a sharp combustible medicine, or with iron.
But if you use a cautery with a combustible medicine, then take a piece of wax, and burn it by extinguishing the ends of it from both sides. And then you should incise the area of the pain on the temple with a lancet, deeply enough for it to be done properly below the skin, so that it is hidden.
And then apply pressure to it with bandages by tightening them securely, and leave that for the space of three hours; and then loosen it and remove the wax, and leave the wound covered for two or three days, and afterwards place a poultice on it soaked in butter until the area becomes warm.
For the treatment of that which is inside, let it be healed with medicine.
And if you wish, use some of the medicines that I have written about in the twelfth chapter on burning medicines.
But when you cauterize with iron according to this method, use fire for the cautery, and this is its form:
and it is called a nail clamp, for its head is in the shape of a nail, with some curvature, and in the middle part of it there is a small protrusion.
And then press on the location of the pain, and hold your hand—so that the artery below is not adhered—and turn the iron slightly little by little with speed.
And if the amount that is adhered due to the curvature is as much as half of it, raise your hand so that the artery below does not adhere, so that there is no bleeding.
And then soak cotton in salt water and place it on the location, and leave it for three days; and afterwards apply honeyed bandages, and subsequently treat with internal medicine to heal.
And if you wish, cauterize at the end of the radius according to the cautery method, and be careful not to cut the artery in this ancient procedure.
Chapter four.
On the cauterization of an ancient ulcer.
When you treat an ulcer as we have described in the previous treatment and in the divisions of diseases, and if it does not improve, and sometimes due to the severity of the disease, neither the first cautery with medicine nor the cautery with fire is sufficient, then it is necessary for you to ignite the radial cautery until it becomes white-hot. Place it on the site of the pain in a line along its length, which is half the width of your finger or slightly more; and then hold your hand steady and press firmly so that it does not cut the artery but penetrates to the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to guard against the continuation of the jawbone, which is curved due to mastication, and that the lizard [muscle] does not adhere and the nerves which move it, and that it does not become spasmodic.
And if it is about the care and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is cut, because in its cutting there is danger, especially for one who does not know what they are doing and is not skilled and experienced; and leave the operation to someone else at the beginning.
And here I will come to the reminder of the management of blood flow from an artery according to the usual method, in its place in this book.
And if you see this illness does not respond to these cautery treatments and the patient's condition is tolerable, cauterize in the appropriate place of the head as we have recounted, and treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you perform the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the rupture of an artery with a cautery having two prongs, this is better cautery and more effective.

On the cautery for ear pains.

Chapter VI.
On the cautery of the turtle.
The one for which treatment and cautery are not used is only of the types that come from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cautery for the type that arises from dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you treat that type of tumor with jars and capipurgi and gargle treatments, and if your treatment does not succeed, then it is necessary to cauterize the disease with three applications: the first at the root of the ear, and the second a little below the temple, and the third at the junction of both lips.
And pause your cauterization at the opposite part of the diseased area, for softening occurs only in the part that appears healthy.
The method of cauterization is that you cauterize there with the cautery on the right side at the extremity of the most prominent ear, and then above the temple, the length of which should be according to the length of a thumb, and then pause your hand with the cautery until the amount equal to half the thickness of the cord is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a special type of knife, the form of which is set forth above. However, even more subtle is that which you see only slightly; and it is necessary to use a knife instead of excessive coarseness, somewhat delicately.
And then treat the area with the liquid that was previously prepared until it is healed.
Chapter VII.
Of the cautery for ancient apoplexy.
When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said and do not cause fever in the patient, then cauterize it with four cauteries: on top of all the temples of their head; and one cauterization on the middle part of the head, as we have said; and one cauterization on the nape. And the method of the cauterizations is done as mentioned above.
And it is cauterized over the mouth of the stomach; and this is better; and then proceed to treat it as appropriate.

Of cauterization for forgetfulness done with live coal.
Give the patient large doses and pills of theriac at the beginning.

Chapter IX.
On the cautery for parasites and the softening of the entire body.
Proceed as you would in the cleansing of the head according to what has been said and what we have mentioned; then shave the head of the patient, and afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle part of the head, and with a cautery over all the parts of the head, and with a cautery on the rear part of it, and with three cauteries along the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the illness of softening the body to do that and the patient can tolerate it and the illness is severe, then cauterize it with four cauteries along the vertebrae of the back, and finally with a cautery inside so that it is covered by the skin, and raise the heat moderately. Then proceed with the treatment until it is healed, and this should be an olive-shaped cautery.
Chapter X.
On the cautery for epilepsy.
An epileptic should not be cauterized unless the epilepsy is caused by phlegm.
And so you should cleanse the brain of the patient at the beginning with herbs and with the other treatment that we have mentioned in the division when the illness is severe and the patient can tolerate the exception of medications.
And if it is a child who does not tolerate the medicines, at that time administer gargles and mouthwashes to clean the mouth, for two or three days, along with the purification of foods.
And then shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize one area with a cautery at the proper location on the head according to the previous method, and another cauterization at the occiput, and over each corner of the head he should cauterize. And if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize with the cauteries that I have mentioned, having paralysis and relaxation of the body over the cervical vertebrae and the thoracic vertebrae.
And let it be an olive cauterization as has been described previously.
But if the patient is a child, then proceed with a gentle cautery according to this method.

On Cauterization for Melancholia.

And then shave the head of the patient, and then apply a well-made trepanation around the circle, and proceed with that at the proper location on the head.
Let the wound be sixty days old, and let it be treated from all sides.
And then apply a liniment; and it is better to use the grease of sheep. And heat that over the fire with moderate warmth according to measure, which the patient can tolerate when it is applied. And then place that in the middle of the head of the patient in a circle, and let it be rubbed in.
And do this once a week for the wound, and follow the regimen until it is healed; or if you prefer, cauterize that in small points according to what is necessary, but have your hand with a cautery properly arranged: this is a special kind of cautery that moistens the brain with moderation.
And then apply that powder mixed in grease or in chicken fat.
Chapter XII.
On the cautery of water descending in the belly.
When it is clear to you the beginning of water in the belly by the signs which I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink what purifies his head, and guard against all humidity for him.

Cut and cauterize all the veins and arteries that you leave for the ligature; and place the cautery at a distance in the region of the temples.
And guard against bleeding when it is cauterized; and if you see any bleeding, stop it with some medicine, which is within your power.

Chapter XIV.
On the cauterization of nasal odor.

Chapter XV.
On Cauteries for Softening the Eyelids of the Eyes.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened due to illness or moisture, then cauterize that eyelid with a cautery in the shape of this lunar cautery; and this is its form:

Chapter XVI.
On Cauteries for the Eyelid of the Eye When the Hairs Turn Inward and Poke the Eye.
When the hairs of the eye turn inward such that they poke the eye, cauterization in those cases is done according to two methods: either by performing it or by using a combustible medicine.
If you cauterize the wound with fire, command the barber to shave around it just as one would for those which are mundane, entering where they are extended and evened out; and if you grasp that of their growth, then wrap them with a bandage so that nothing is left before the hair grows back.
Once they have grown back and evened out, then place the head of the patient in your lap, and gently press upon the eyelids over the wound with a probe, marked as according to the shape of a leaf of mercury, and let the beginning of the mark be near the hair.
And then place a small piece of linen or mucilage of fine flour on the wound.
And then apply the cautery, which this is the form of.
And then cauterize over the figure that you have marked, little by little, in small stages, until the surface of the area which is like a myrtle leaf is completely burned through properly.
And the sign of health in your work is that you see the eyelid of the wound already contracted and the hair around it raised above the puncture.
And then raise your hand and lay it upon that for three days, and afterwards place a piece of cloth over it until the scar is remedied. And then care for that until it is healed.
But if the hair around it becomes affected near its growth and the eyelid is softened, then perform the cautery on that again just as you did initially.
If there are hairs inside the lower eyelid, then at that time cauterize it so that it is raised to its natural place and healed, and that the hairs do not touch the eye.
You should cauterize with a burning medicine in this case; command the patient to pull out the hairs until they are long and healed, and then make it from paper or cloth in the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And then take known soap and one ounce of a living herb, or something similar to it, and mix those ingredients well, and apply it quickly so that it is not rubbed; then spread this over the paper which is made as the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it on both eyes; and place under each eye wrapped in clean cloth, and have the patient's head in your lap.
And place your finger on the medicine and press it slightly so that the patient feels the sting of the medicine, for this sting is like that of fire.
And when the patient perceives the stinging sensation, then remove the medicine and wash it with your finger; once the stinging stops, then wash the eye with water. And now check if the eyelid is raised as it should be; if so, you can proceed with cautery or incision, for this is good progress. If not, return to applying the medicine to a different location where it has not been applied yet and do not allow it to darken until it heals and the eye returns to its proper state.
And then place it on the affected area at the border until the condition of the irritation is eradicated, and then treat it with healing medication or another remedy until it is healed.
It is necessary for you to guard your operation with vigilant diligence so that no part of the medicine falls into the eye. And if after some days the eyelid has become softened and any cause of hair pulling in the eye, then again apply your medicine to that place where the eyelid has softened, and properly as you did at the beginning, and soon within it will be healed.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And you should know that the eyes of people vary in size and smallness, and therefore according to this, your treatment is adjusted.
And the way to truth in this art will not be hidden from one who studies in this field.
Chapter XVII.
On Cauterization of a Fistula in the Lacrimal Region of the Eye.
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not confer with your treatment, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method: instruct the patient to place his head on your lap, and hold the patient's head steady between your hands in such a way that it does not move or shake.
And then place a piece of cloth soaked in egg white or in a paste of flour over the eye of the patient.
And then heat the cautery, which has this form:
which is made of copper, similar in shape to a reed or the quill of an eagle, with one end shaped like the cautery.
And if you wish, enter into the other extremity. And if you want it to be as soft as a sponge.
But he who is concave is better for the task at hand.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and let it drain and dry it out. And if it is not open, now open it and extract the corruption from it.
And then press on it with the cautery which should be well heated, and place it there but a little, so that you do not miss your hand or the wound become agitated, and now place the cautery in the flesh of the nose and burn that.
And thus if at the beginning of your cauterization it penetrates to the bone, that is good; and if not, now repeat the cautery once or twice, as needed; and leave it thus for three days, and then press on that wound gently and around it apply a drying agent until it is healed.
But if after these days it has not healed, now apply to it acute corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and proceed as necessary according to its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula which they first described as follows: enter the location of the fistula and clean it, and then place in that fissure finely powdered material according to its form. And pour into it one ounce of melted lead; and with your hand gently but firmly, so that the wound does not become agitated because the melted lead should not reach the flesh around it; and ensure that you press on the wound’s surface covered in egg white or water, for lead adheres to the location of the fistula and heals it miraculously.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, that is well; but otherwise, it is necessary to administer nasal trephination and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose according to how it will come into its proper place.

Chapter XX.
On the cauterization of teeth and the softening of gums.

And then remove your hand, and shortly afterward repeat the cautery several times as you wish.

Chapter XXI.

From there, apply hot cloths until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you do so, soak wool or cloth in the aforementioned broth, and place that on the aching tooth, and place over it an iron heated until the iron reaches the pain of the tooth's root.
However, for cautery with fire, you should attend to the thickness of the skin or flesh, and place it in the middle of some thickness so that the intensity of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then heat the cautery to the desired temperature, and place it on the tooth with your hand until the cautery is rubbed on it; do this several times as long as the pain persists either on that day or the next day.
And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good broth due to the pressure of that cautery and hold it for an hour, then spit it out; this is how the cautery should be used.
And cauterize as much as you wish, according to what is possible for you.

Chapter XXVIII.
On the puncturing of an abscess of the kidney with a cautery.

Therefore, have the patient lie on his back; and then identify the location of the abscess by probing; and subsequently use the cautery which resembles a reed, the form of which was described on the previous page. such that it is round and emits sparks. And then return the bowels or cloth to their original position, and then place your hand over the area to prevent them from escaping.
And once you have placed the patient between the sheets and left one sheet over them, another should be placed under their buttocks, and another under their feet, while they lie on their back.
And then place the cautery on that mark with your hand holding the cautery straight, and do so until you feel the bone of the pubis in the middle; repeat this several times if you did not succeed on the first attempt to locate the bone.
Observe wisely the condition of the bowel at the time of your cautery, that you do not burn that bowel such that it does not bring about death or some great harm to the patient.
And be aware that when you perform the cautery, do not touch the bone, do not proceed with your operation.
And it is necessary that the cautery for children be gentle according to their age and size.
And take care of the site of the cautery for three days, bandaging it so that the fire scar heals.
And subsequently take care of that with other ointments until it is healed.
And let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the site is sealed and the wound healed.
And it is necessary to restrict the patient's diet according to the duration of the treatment period during which the inflammation of the abdomen occurs, and that the bowel does not protrude due to the effort of healing.
And subsequently, when it is time to remove the dressing after forty days, administer it carefully and properly, and keep that area bandaged for another forty days.
And let them be restricted from work and overeating food and drink, and from speaking loudly, for when they follow this complete regimen of healing, they will be healed.
And I will describe the treatment of ruptures in other parts of the abdomen, and at the beginning, if you do not want them to spread, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size; let it be as much as is taken from the cord, as one third of it. And subsequently treat that as we have said, and it will not be adjusted.
And some of the earlier writers said that rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery according to this form, as it is marked with a template:
and a line is drawn which you follow latitudinally on the abdomen above the rupture, and another line above it; then place your hand with a nail-shaped cautery, but the first cautery is faster and better.
Chapter XLVI.
On the Cauterization of Torticollis.
When you find in some members due to falling or striking there is pain that persists for a long time and does not improve with medication, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And the cautery for each member should be according to its size and smallness, its strength and weakness, and the location of the torticollis and the pain.
If he is healed by the first cautery, that is good; but if not, then repeat the cautery on it. For it is customary for such pains to be punctured from one member to another nearby one, so you must achieve this with the cautery until the patient is healed.
Chapter XLVII.
On the Cauterization of Leprosy.
Some cases of leprosy are greatly helped by cautery, but rarely when the type of leprosy is caused by the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
And so when you want to cauterize that patient, consider whether the leprosy is commencing and can be cured with what we have mentioned in the division and do not say it will not happen, and if you fear for the patient that the corruption may spread throughout their body and complexion, then cauterize him on his head with five cauteries: one at the middle of the head, and another lower down; both above the ears; and one behind, over the nape or back of the neck.
And lastly your hand should apply the cautery a little inside where it presses upon the bone, thereby displacing the scabs, so that the expulsion of thick vapors may be facilitated from there; and cauterize over the wound as is necessary.
And if leprosy has already spread over the body and is clearly manifest, then you should cauterize it with those cauteries which we have mentioned at the beginning; and apply one cautery on the tip of the nose, two cauteries on each cheek, two on each cervical vertebra, six on the dorsal vertebrae, a large one near the lumbar region, another on the buttocks, two on each thigh, one on each ankle, two on each elbow, one on each wrist, and two on each calf muscle; cauterize it also over all the joints of the hands and feet, as well as on each heel, and at the axillae.
And be careful of the nerves that run over the heel so as not to burn them.
And in some cases it is cauterized with one cautery on the bone of the little toe and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you apply cauteries appropriately, the more helpful and beneficial they are; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as others would, because the body is already numb.
And it is appropriate that the cauteries be large or small according to the members and joints as dictated by the nature of the tools.
Regarding the treatment with cautery, use flour of oats mixed with honey. For the other cure, ensure it leads to healing.
Chapter XLVIII.
On the cautery for stupor.
When a limb is numb or asleep and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but does not heal, then you should cauterize that numb limb using cautery appropriate to the size of the limb or its smallness.
And let the heat of the cautery be moderate, entering slightly beneath the surface. And subsequently treat that area with an ointment so that it may heal.
And sometimes a cautery is applied to a numb area that extends deeper into the muscles and vertebrae, as well as along the course of the nerves that control that limb, to alleviate the numbness.
But do not proceed with this unless you are knowledgeable about the anatomy of the limb and the course of the nerves throughout the moving body.
Chapter XLIX.
On the cautery for wounds that become paralyzed.
When an old wound does not respond to any of the medicinal ointments, then you should cauterize over that area using a cautery slightly heated according to the quantity and nature of the tissue until the whiteness and color of the wound are alleviated, and its color changes.
And subsequently treat that area with flour of oats and lentils mixed with rose oil and leaves of arnica, and either dove blood or swallow blood, taking an equal part of each and thoroughly mixing them together. Then apply a cloth soaked in this mixture to the affected area until it heals.
Chapter I.
On cauterizing ulcers.
When cancer begins and you want to remove it, then cauterize that part with a cauterizing agent in the form of a circle around it as it appears.
And the wise ones say that it should be cauterized with the last cauterization in the middle area; but I have not seen this done, for I fear that it may become ulcerated, and I have seen this happen in some cases.
It is safer to cauterize around the affected area in a circular manner as we have said, or in other words, use cautery around it.
Chapter II.
On cauterizing abcesses.
When an abscess is delayed in maturation due to excessive moisture in that area, or because of the patient's condition, such as being old and weak, having little blood, or due to time, and you want to hasten the maturation of the abscess; then cauterize around it with small punctures using a cautery; and afterwards it will mature more quickly.
But if you want to pierce the abscess with a cautery, then choose a cautery that is suitable for this purpose; and place it in the middle of the abscess until it penetrates the tissue.
And if the cautery is applied to a location that is further away to spare the arm from excessive pain; and then care for it until it heals.
Chapter LII.
On Cauterization with Corrosives.
Corrosives are a wandering corruption in the limb, which corrodes as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, when you see the corrosive in a place where it can withstand cautery with fire, then ignite and cauterize small and large areas as is appropriate in the place where the corrosion is.
And proceed to cauterize it from all sides until you eradicate all the corrosion and leave no cause for it to remain.
And then dress it for three days, and apply poultices to the cauterized areas thrice daily with an oil mixture until all the scars are eradicated and all the corruption is gone.
And then treat it with substances that promote flesh growth.
But if after three days you see that healthy flesh is growing where there is no corruption, it is good; but if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains in the corrupted areas.
And some corrosives are treated with sharp medicines, for these are suitable as an alternative to cautery. But cauterization with fire is more quickly effective.
And I have already mentioned the treatment of it with sharp medicines in the division, and therefore use that when you find it necessary.
Chapter LIII.
On cauterization of wounds and other similar cases.
Most often, in the parts below the knee where a condition called clau maladie occurs, which is caused by thick and hardened flesh that affects the foot; and one should cauterize it in two ways, namely with fire and with hot water.
The cauterization with fire is done by heating the cauterizing instrument concave in shape like a ring, which is made of iron according to the quantity that contains the clau condition throughout all parts, and it should be finely polished.
And then place the heated instrument on the clau, and then move your hand with the cauterizing tool around the perimeter of the clau until the cauterization reaches the depth of the clau. And let it be for three days until it begins to form scabs. And then apply a poultice made of crushed wild mallows mixed with salt to it, and leave the poultice on for one night, as this will help eradicate it from its roots.
And then treat the area with a generative flesh ointment until it is healed.
And if it does not convert, and often happens on the surface of the body, especially in the muscles and skin, then you should administer cauterization with hot water. This is done by taking a small tube made of earthenware or iron or ring-shaped, and place it on the clau; then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube and hold your hand around it tightly, revolving it with compression from all sides, and apply the edge of the tube to the root of the clau, allowing the hot water to penetrate through the root of the clau; wait for the malady to be affected by the heat of the water for about an hour, then remove it, as the clau along with its roots will be eradicated.
And thus place one against the other until you come upon all of them in their proper order in the body.
And place next to the care of those abscesses that the roots of the nails have been eradicated with the help of those medicines which cause the flesh to grow.
Chapter LIII.
On the cautery for tremors.
When you find a tremor due to irritation of the nerves or from fever caused by irritation, or from some similar cause, it is then necessary for you to cauterize that area with four cauteries or five on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra one cauterization; and at the joints of the legs, and over the stomach, use an olive-shaped cauterization.
And the tremor subsides and the health improves quickly from the irritation of the illness.
Chapter LIV.
On the cautery for accidental injuries to the body.
When there are accidental wounds in the body that have become pus-filled and cracked, formed from thick, corrupted matter; therefore, at the beginning when they appear, it is necessary to cauterize over the entire fistula with a fine cautery made of myrtle wood, the tip of which is exposed to fire; or with the long thorns of erestologia; or with a lentil-shaped cautery.
And sometimes it is necessary to cauterize immediately at the beginning of its expulsion according to this method; and if not done so, the excess matter that causes these issues will be disrupted, and thus they heal from them.
However, it is necessary that this be done immediately after evacuation and phlebotomy.
Chapter LX.
On cauterization of blood flow due to accidental cutting of an artery.
If the flow of blood from an artery that has been cut is due to a plague that originated inside, or due to the beginning of abscesses or cauterization of the limb, and similar cases, it is difficult to remedy this.
When such a situation occurs, quickly apply your hand to the opening of the artery, and press on it with enough strength to hold the clot inside until the blood flow stops, and do not let it escape.
And then place in the fire olive coals, both small and large, for many pieces, and blow on them until they are ignited.
And then take one of those coals, either small or large depending on the location and condition in which the artery is ruptured, and place it quickly over the vein after you have removed your hand, so that the cauterization stops and restricts the blood.
And if the blood is expelled from the opening of the artery when you remove your hand and extract the cauterization tool, then take another coal quickly from those coals which are prepared in the fire, and continue doing this one after another until the blood flow is stopped.
And be careful not to burn the nerve that is here, and ensure it does not cause other harm.
And know that when blood flows from an artery, it is not possible then to restrain the blood, especially when the artery is large, unless one employs one of four methods: either by cauterization as we have mentioned, or by extraction, because when it is extracted, the extremities are burned and the blood is restrained; or let it be bound with astringent medicines, or let it rest upon medicines whose virtue is to restrict the blood; and they should be strengthened with poultices with moderate pressure.
And let him who administers moderate binding with bandages and compression with cloths or by the position of burning materials and similar methods not hurry but proceed slowly.
And if this happens to someone and there is no doctor present or medicine, then gently place the index finger on the opening of that vein as we have said, and understand that due to great constriction within, the blood remains in the upper part of the wound, and the finger should not be moved from the artery; and above the artery it should be sprinkled with cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened; and then proceed with cauterization or medicine as necessary.
Of incision and puncture and wound treatment and of phlebotomy and of wounds and their similar conditions.
We have already said in the first chapter about every illness in which cauterization with fire is appropriate and with burning medicine, and the occasions and causes for it, and the instruments necessary for the forms of cauterizations; and I have arranged the chapters on the superiority of the head among the parts of the body.
In this procedure described in this chapter by that method, may God bless the one asking about it, at the time concerning what they have asked.
And before I begin this, listen, son, and learn that in this chapter it is by fear as it is in the first chapter on cauterization.
And for this reason, it is necessary to be in great caution, because in the operation which is in this chapter many times there is evacuation of blood or pus, which can endanger life due to the application of heat on a vein or incision over an abscess or opening of an exit or purging of a plague or extraction of a splinter or stone and similar procedures. And with all of those actions, accompany fear and trembling, and in the worst case of their danger, death.
And I warn you that upon you does not fall what is mentioned in the context of danger, for some times such cases can be caused by methods used by people dealing with many types of illnesses. And among them are some who become enraged by their illness and die quickly because of the severity of what they find in their illness, and due to the length of their illness, and this illness brings fear which signifies death.
And among them is one who gives away his possessions and says, "I hope for health from this," while their actual illness is fatal.
And therefore, you must not consent to those who come to you with this method; and your caution should be greater than your greed and rapacity; and do not assume any reason for it beyond certain knowledge that confirms what affects you, and to which a reputable succession of practice attests.
For the treatment of all your patients, make a prognosis and indication as to which one is likely to be cured, for in that you will have assistance in acquiring fame and reputation, praise and glory.
O, children, may God inspire your mind and not take from you direction and protection, for this is in His power.
And I have arranged this chapter distinctly by chapters as it follows the chapter on cauterization, concerning the treatment of the head among other things, so that you may be pleased with what you seek regarding this and what you need.
First Chapter.
On the treatment of water that is contained in the head of children.
Know that this illness often affects children shortly after birth when the nurse presses too hard on the child's head.
And sometimes it happens for hidden causes that are not known.
But I have seen this illness only in children; and in all those whom I saw it led to death, and thus it appeared to me as a fatal condition.
And I have seen a child whose head was filled with water, and the size of his head was so enlarged that he could not control it due to the greatness of his head, and before long the moisture increased within until it caused death.
And this moisture is either accumulated between the skin and the bone, or it is accumulated below the bone on the skull.
For when the operation is to be performed and the moisture lies between the bone and the boil, which is small, you should cut in the middle of the head with a slit in length, and let the length of this slit extend two fingers' breadth where the moisture flows, and this is the form of the spatum:
And if the moisture is more increased and the boil is larger, then at this time there should be two slits according to this method:
And if the moisture is deeper than the bone, the sign of this is that you see the commissures of the head covered all around and the water is squeezed out when you press it with your finger at the sides but not from underneath. You should cut in the middle of the head with three slits according to this method:
and immediately the incision should extract all the moisture; and then dress the slits with cloths and plasters; and subsequently apply poultices of oil and vinegar over them for five days, and then loosen the bandage and treat the wound with lint and ointments, and dress the head symmetrically; and eat food that is dry with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
And there is another method of incision, which you should consider according to the size of the boil and the collection of water, for sometimes it may be in the occipital region, or in the front part, or on the right, or on the left; and therefore attend to the incision where the boil appears and the swelling of the water, and do this according to what is best possible for you.
And observe that you do not cut the artery and avoid excessive bleeding, for the illness may worsen due to that loss of blood along with the evacuation of moisture.
Chapter Second.
When I come to certain carbuncles or boils on the thighs or in the genitals, and if it is old and not responsive to treatment with medicines, then at that time the last resort is to cut into those two arteries.
And therefore, when you want to incise those arteries, have the patient raise his hand and rub the area with a rough cloth so that the arteries become visible; then secure the patient's neck with a cloth; and examine where the vein can be pressed; these locations are near the ears, but they may vary in some people.
And then press on the artery with your finger, and then incise each one with a sharp scalpel, piercing into the bone, and do this across the width of the head.
And if you wish, insert the scalpel below the artery and cut it at the points where the incisions are above.
And the length of the incision should be about two fingers wide, for when an artery is cut, the blood flows out in a pulsating manner, often spouting frequently.
But if the artery does not appear upon inspection, then measure three finger breadths from the ear, and then press with your finger to find it, and make an incision into the bone.
In order to extract and treat pus from a wound, take one ounce of vinegar, and it is light enough to pour out like wheat or bran, and all this is according to the quantity which appears appropriate for the strength of the patient and the fullness of the vein.
And then consider the wound, and if there remains any cause of pus above the bone, now incise that so that it does not become an abscess from cauterization.
And then strengthen the wound with poultices and bandages of linen cloth, and afterward care for it with ointments until it is healed.
Chapter III.
On the extraction of veins that are in the temples.
When it happens that someone suffers from migraines or acute headaches due to excessive humidity in the body and qualities in the veins of the temples, or if they are similar severe conditions, and treatment with medical methods does not provide relief, then we resort to these diseases the extraction of veins in the temples, or cauterization of those as we have shown.
And the method of the operation and extraction of those veins is that the patient shaves the hair which is on the temples; and identify the visible vein in the temple as it is shown by its pulse, and it is hidden from most people due to the force of friction.
And if it is hidden from you, then tie the head of the patient with some cloth; and afterward rub the area with a rough cloth or evaporate the area with hot water until the vein becomes clearly visible. And now you take the spatula which has this form: And then you peel the membrane in such a way that you reach the artery; and there remove it and extract it to the appropriate places until you extract it from the membrane and reveal those tunics which are underneath, from every part.
But if the artery is fine, now wrap it at its extremity with a ligature, and then cut off a part according to the quantity by which the ends of it are stretched out and contracted, and there will be no flow of blood, for if they are not thus divided the blood would not rise.
And then remove the blood from the wound in quantity of one ounce up to three.
And if the artery is large, now make sure you tie it in two places with a very strong thread or cords at a distance, and do not allow it to become putrid before the healing of the wound and prevent the flow of blood.
And then cut away the excess which is between two ligatures; and do this either at that hour or another time.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cautery to the bone with a knife cautery until the ends of it are divided, and this will serve as that work.
And it is better to do this when the patient has a fever or is of hot complexion; for cautery is one of those causes that help to dry up excessive moisture, and therefore it is better in such conditions.
Concerning the extraction of arteries, ensure that the place where it will be done is clean and proper, and let them lie on a decently prepared poultice, and nearby have medicines ready that cause flesh to grow and bandages so that it may be healed.
And if while you are working some other place bleeding occurs from the artery, then you should proceed to constrict that blood, either with cautery or by filling the place with cloth, and press your hand in so that the blood may be restrained. And if none of those causes are present to you, then press your hand over the place until the blood is congealed, and cover the area with water of extreme coldness until the pain subsides, and bind it as necessary.
And what is most important in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery having two cloths, after you have marked both places with a needle, and then place some ignited material inside until it reaches the bone and severs the vein at two points, so that you can stretch what is between its extremities, as they are not fully consolidated by this cautery.
And this is the form of the cautery:
And the sharpness of the two cloths should be noted. However, if the sharpness is such that two knives are better, for if as sharp as two knives approaches each fracture, and do not cut through the flesh too quickly.
Therefore, when there is any swelling in those areas, the heat of the fire is applied to them and the flesh is cut away quickly.
And this method is better than all methods and faster.
And let the space between two knives be the quantity of the thickness of a finger.
Chapter four.
On the treatment of sharp and acidic tears from the eyes.
When such acidic tears occur, and the cause is from those veins which are above the head on the outside, and if there is no clear reason for the treatment with medicine, sometimes the face of the patient turns red, and a sensation as if ants were crawling in their forehead can be felt, and the eyes are so weakened that even their eyelashes can barely be seen, and the eyelids are scorched by the sharpness of the tears. The ancient practitioners used to treat such cases with this procedure without delay.
And you command the patient to pluck the hairs that are on their forehead, and then cut three incisions equally spaced according to the length of the forehead. And if the length of the incision is about two fingers: one incision should be equally distant from the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, and the second according to the length a little behind the movement of the tears that flow through the lacrimal duct, and the third on the other side.
And guard against the beginning of the arteries, which are on both sides, and extend your hand along the continuation of both jaws. And if the space between each incision is the quantity of three such adjustments.
And if you have a piece of prepared sponge or dried cloth with which you can dry the blood.
And then insert the spatula between two sharp points, which is the shape of the incision as follows: which is from the first part of the template to the second incision. Excise from there all the tissue that is between two incisions at the suture which is on the bone, and then make this median incision to the second incision. And then place this spatula and insert another instrument called a knife, sharp on one side and not sharp on the other, into the first incision.
And place the sharp side on the flesh and adjacent tissue, and the blunt side against the bone, and insert it until you reach the median fissure, and dissect all the vessels that descend from the head to the heels.
But ensure that the incision continues to appear on the tissue, and then make this in the median fissure to the other fissure.
And when the flow of blood is equal in quantity, press the places where clotted blood has collected.
And then place small pieces of old wood in each fissure, and apply powder mixed with vinegar and oil on them, and bandages so that no abscess forms by cauterization.
And on the third day remove the bandage and administer great infusion of hot water or terebinth, and afterwards treat with an ointment of basilicon and rose oil and other ingredients until the wounds are healed.
Chapter 5.
On the treatment of tumors by catharsis and the expulsion of humors descending from the inner parts of the head.
When there is acute and continuous bleeding from catharsis, and the humors of the patient are exhausted and small, and their care shows weakness, and the eyelids are ulcerated with hair loss in their place, and there is sharp pain and extreme drying at the forehead, then you should understand from these symptoms that the matter and catharsis do not come except from veins proceeding from inner parts.
And the best treatment for these conditions is as follows: Command the patient to shave their forehead, and then make a small incision at the middle of the forehead (beginning from the midpoint between the left temple and the right temple; ensure that this incision reaches the bone; extend your hand from the temples which are far apart due to chewing), until the bone is exposed.
Dry all the blood with a sponge or a dry cloth, and then apply a mixture between the two edges of the incision with yellow wax or strips of cloth. And then apply dry powdered herbs mixed with wine and oil on top so that it does not lead to an infected wound.
And when you remove this and see that the abscess has already diminished, then scrape the bone where new flesh begins to grow, and afterwards treat it with a drying regimen that promotes the growth of new flesh. For example, take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colocynth, mix them together, and make a plaster from it to be applied to these wounds where new flesh is growing.
Chapter VI.
On the treatment of what affects the ears.
Any cause that affects the ears is one of four types: it may be a mineral stone or something resembling a stone, such as iron or wood; or it may come from a plant, such as thorns or beans; or it may be a fluid-like substance, such as water and vinegar or similar liquids; or it may be some kind of animal.
And when a stone is lodged in the ear or any other cause similar to those that do not adhere or are embedded in the ear, place the ear towards the sun, and if you see the stone, then administer some drops of violet oil or sesame oil, and shortly after induce sneezing with appropriate conditions, and plug the nose at the moment of sneezing. And then place around the ear some pieces of cloth or wool, and extend the ear towards the upper parts, as this treatment is often effective for such causes.
And if it is not expelled, then administer an extract with the instrument called gesti epicicarios, which is a subtle tool of this form:
And if it is expelled with the instrument, that is good; and if not, then administer an extract along with a slight amount of repeated application.
And if it is not expelled by these methods, then make a tube of reed and insert the end of the tube into the ear canal, and seal around the tube with wax and softened oil so that only the tube remains open. From there extract the vein with strong traction, for troops watched as we have recounted.
If it is not forcibly done in this manner, then take a thin thread or a piece of equipment with which birds are caught, a small amount, and place that at the end of the vein, and then wrap around that knot gently placed. And then insert it into the ear canal with ease, and then dry the ear of its moisture.
And if it is not forcibly done for all the causes that we have recounted, then you should proceed to cut in front of where it becomes an abscess or spasm.
And the method of cutting it is that you first lance the vein called sephasica and extract the blood according to the manner of its virtue, and then make a small incision between your fingers and turn the ear towards above, and make a slight cut at the edge of the ear where it is most pressed. And let the cut be in a crescent shape until it reaches the stone, and when the stone is found, remove it if you can with appropriate instruments; then close the cut quickly at that moment, and care for it until it is healed.
And if the cause lying in the ear is one of the gristles that grow and become inflamed, then administer the treatment and the extraction of it; but if you do not obey this method, then take fine wax as follows: and administer the removal of that gristle which is lodged in the ear.
If you do not want to use water when you think that it is already moistened by the vapor from the air, place it in various positions, and draw out therefrom with hooks or subtle gestures, or as we have said concerning incision, for the extraction is easier.
In the water that has entered the ear, it is useful for the patient to use sneezing at the beginning with certain preparations, and fill one side of their ear with some old cotton, and place on the affected ear, if by this method it is expelled, good; but if not, now take small pebbles or stones according to the length of a finger, and heat those in the fire for a little while, and the patient should insert one of them into the ear canal and jump with one side of their body onto that stone and strike another stone on the stone inside the ear. Do not remove the stone until all the water has been expelled.
Do not remove the stone until all the water has been expelled. And the water will be expelled in this way: take paper or wool, and place one end of it in the ear while holding the other end over fire until it is partially burned.
And place another piece of wool and do this as many times as necessary until all the water is expelled, and then probe it with a cannula as was said about the stone extractor.
In the extraction of an animal that has entered the ear, if it is a small creature, treat it similarly as we have said in the division; but if it is a larger one causing pain to the patient, then administer the extraction with gestures and hooks, and the cause of this is more urgent than all other causes that occur in the ear.
In the extraction of worms generated in the ear, when you treat it with that which we have said in the division and in the tractate on distillations and do not confirm your treatment, then it is necessary to expose the ear to the sun.
And therefore, if any cause of the worms appears, then extract it with gentle movements or subtle instruments; but if no cause appears, then take a cannula that is narrow below and wide above, and this is its shape: And insert the delicate end into the ear according to the amount that you can bear; then suck with force using that instrument several times until all the worms are expelled.
But if you do not obey this instruction, then pack and seal around the cannula with wax as we have said; then administer distillations that have already proven effective in the treatment of worms, which you will find described in the tractate on distillations.
And make your application with the instrument through which you pour medicinal oils into the ear, and this is its shape: And make it of silver or ivory, narrow at the bottom, with a small tube and a flat top.
And it should be like pressing against the concavity of the cannula where it will be necessary. And if you wish, take a reed and wrap its end neatly with cloth, then pour oil into the concavity of the ear or juice from some herb, or any of these medicines into the cannula — which is in the ear —, and then insert the reed with the cloth at the top and press it gently so that the oil is expelled into the concavity of the hearing and the patient feels the oil inside.
And let that which is to be inserted into the ear be first heated over the fire a little. And be careful that the cause for which you will distill into the ear is not too rough, for medicines for the ear do not tolerate this.
Chapter VII.
On the treatment of blocked ears.
Sometimes infants are born from their mothers' wombs with unopened ears, and this also happens in some adults, where the ear canal is blocked by infection or flesh growing there; and this blockage sometimes occurs at the entrance of the ear canal, which cannot be seen clearly, and sometimes it is in the outer parts.
And that which occurs at the entrance of the ear, which cannot be seen clearly, is in the most difficult conditions to heal.
And in that case where you can see clearly, place the ear of the patient in the sun and observe it. And if you see a blockage that is apparent, open it with a fine spatula of this form:
If the end of it where the width is small, of which one part is sharp and the other is not; and the spatula should be of two thin sides so that it does not cause injury to the ear.
And if the blockage is due to flesh growing in the ear or in the ear canal, then use fine scissors and carefully cut away all the excess flesh inside.
And if there is an obstruction in the ear canal, then take a thin reed and heat that in the fire for a little while, and then place that into the ear canal.
And if you feel an obstruction with what the patient identifies as easy to reach due to hearing difficulty, apply pressure to expel it; and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.
And then place in the ear a piece of cloth according to the quantity of the mass that you have wrapped in Egyptian cotton; and do this for several days until you are sure of the consolidation of the lesion; or take something and dip it in rose water and sprinkle it with finely ground powder and use it; and if you see the ear already inflamed, then you should remove what was there and replace it with another piece wrapped in wax mixed with olive oil, until the inflammation subsides; and then continue treatment until it is healed.
But if there is a flow of blood, then soak a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use another treatment that stops the bleeding, which is described in the chapter on distillation.
Chapter VIII.
On the treatment of inflammation that occurs on the eyelids.
Inflammation that occurs on the eyelids of the eyes is sometimes moist, and at other times it is dry.
Therefore, you should have those available in small jars or containers, and grind them finely from their roots, and then apply them as a powder to the affected areas.
If there is pain and bleeding from a vein, then at that hour you should cauterize those places with a cautery of fine antimony.
And the best cauterization is near the incisions and troops that return when there remains some cause for them; and when they are cauterized with fire, those causes are consumed and do not return.
Chapter IX.
Treatment for a condition that affects the eyelids.
Recurrent causes are hidden in the eyelids, some of which resemble a severe condition in their strength and hardness, and therefore this severity is called.
And it is an aggregation of thick humidity in the eyelid, both below and above.
Therefore, the operation in such cases is to consider at that moment whether the condition has arisen from what appears on the eyelid and is spread throughout; and the cause of it is superficial.
Therefore, apply something over that place along the length of the fissure, and then carefully remove it from all parts with ease until it is clean, and then suspend it with an ointment and cover it.
And if the condition is severe, then you adjust it with stitches; and take care of it until it is healed.
And if it is mild, it will not cause harm because the warmth of treatment restores and heals it.
And if the swelling is inclining towards the inner parts of the eyelid, you should lift up its surface, then hold the eyelid and suspend the swelling with a needle, another that you need from the beginning, and press it from all sides, and if the eyelid because of incision is lengthened, this do not notice in any way.
And after the incision, wash the wound with salt water; and treat the area with something that heals so that it may be healed.
Chapter 10.
On the treatment around the eye above the wound.
Swelling occurs in the area above the eyelids, mainly affecting children, worsening their wounds and causing them great pain; they cannot look at the brightness of the sun because tears continuously flow from their eyes.
And because of this, you see them lying with their faces covered all the time, and they sleep with their faces down; and above their lower eyelids are moist eyebrows, which have been covered by inflammation, and there is a clear sign of swelling in the eye; and when you press the area with your fingers, you feel swelling inside.
And there is a method of treatment where the patient places their head in your lap, and you place a cloth over them and make a circle according to the quantity that contains blood from all parts, and then place it on top and press with your fingers all around so that swelling aggregates at the center of the circle, and then apply moisture to the center of that area using a spatula inserted into a small incision along its length, but ensure that this incision is not larger than the one made in phlebotomy.
In the middle of the incision you should cut the cartilage completely until you reach the pleura, for in major operations the pleura is exposed by a rupture according to the form of the rib cavity.
Then extract that which you wrapped in the cloths between your fingers at the parts from inside until it is dispersed.
And be careful not to probe into the rupture so that you do not reach the lung, and avoid doing that.
But if the pleura does not appear at the beginning of the rupture, then probe into the rupture slightly with ease until you encounter the pleura; and then extract it as we have said; and then dip cloths in water and vinegar and place them over the area and press them down with dust.
And some people use salt and place it in the deepest part of the rupture so that what remains is dried by this humidity.
And then take care of it until it is healed.
But if an abscess occurs in the area, then treat it with gentle plasters until it is healed.
Chapter XI.

Chapter XII.
On the elevation of hairs in the groin with forceps when the hair is hard.
When the hairs are unnatural, hard, rough, and prickly in the groin, then you should take fine forceps and place them on that part gently and carefully, adjusting the extremities of the hair so each is grasped subtly. And let the length of the forceps be about the width of one palm.
And then you prepare another fine forceps briefly, and grasp the extremities of that hair if you wish.
And then place the patient in a suitable position in the light, and let it be close to the sun so that your work is clear, for this is a subtle and delicate operation.
And then insert the needle into the root of the grasped hair which requires extraction, and make it penetrate quickly until you pull it out from above the natural hair.
And then pull the hair out from above and insert it into an alcohol solution, and let there be one or two or three hairs and no more.
And then pull your hand away so that the hair is completely removed along with the alcohol solution from the root of the natural hair.
But if the alcohol solution is drawn out and the hair is not removed, pull the alcohol solution away from the surrounding area with the forceps you have prepared for that purpose, so that it is fully extracted along with the excess tissue.
From the wound of the eye, one should first remove any foreign bodies and fragments from it, and then allow the edges of the wound to heal together with clamps for two or three days, until the hair adheres at its place and grows over that good flesh.
And if the hair is too short, then you should take a longer hair from among the natural hairs and place it there, or let it grow until it reaches an appropriate length, and then lift that hair.
Chapter XIII.
On the treatment of a boil that appears on the upper eyelid.
When a boil appears in the eye and causes contraction of the eyelid when it is closed, either to the right or to the left side, due to poor healing of a wound, surgery, or cautery, it is called leporine. This boil may be either natural or accidental, caused by poor healing of wounds, surgeries, or cauterizations, or similar neglect in treatment.
The method of the procedure is that you should cut open that contraction and separate its edges, and place between them a piece of linen cloth, and bind it until it heals.
And it is not advisable to use treatments that dry out or constrain the area; for if you do this, the boil will return worse than before and never heal properly.
Use treatments that soften and mollify, such as fenugreek; boil it in water along with its seeds or juice from the plant, which is dissolved in some oil, then soak a piece of cloth in this mixture and apply it to the area.
The treasure of your cure is that you should pierce every bud that is not consolidated according to the form at the beginning.
And this operation which we have mentioned is nothing but a correction of the halezacrati that does not return to its original form as it was before.
Chapter XIV.
On the treatment of ehacrati which is performed on the lower eyelid.
This alzacratium which is made on the lower eyelid, which is properly called alzacratium; and it is of two kinds, one natural, the other accidental.
The accidental one is caused by trauma or by a cut or by cautery or by other similar causes.

And then stretch the flesh at the parts above with the needle and cut along it with a broad spatula. This is the Greek letter: lambda.
And cut the flesh there in the amount equal to the length of the upper eyelid before it, that which will heal as the eyelid.
And then adjust the separated parts and sew them together with linen thread; and then treat those with what we have said about softening medicines and warm compresses until they are healed.
And if you need to incise across a crack or suture or cauterize, now it is necessary for you to make an incision in a straight line over the eyelash follicles as was described. And then separate the poultice between two layers as we have said.
In the summary of the sermon on the treatment of incisions when they are above or below, let it run according to the operation, as it is prepared in the form of an incision, and that is in a variety of shapes.
